## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws and temperature through thermal softening mechanisms. The interplay between mechanical deformation and thermal effects is central to materials science.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated softening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Temperature-dependent Ludwik: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik with exponential thermal factor)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power law for pre-strained materials)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Thermal-strain coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * (c2 - T)) (Arrhenius-type temperature dependence of modulus)
- Homologous temperature model: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (power-law thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) to capture stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Linear thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiply strain-dependent term by (c0 - c1*T) factor
- Thermally activated processes → exp(c0 / T) or exp(-c0 * T) terms reflecting Boltzmann-type thermal activation
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening begins
- Homologous temperature scaling → (T_melt - T)**c power-law form capturing melting-point-referenced softening
- Strain-temperature interaction → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 capturing coupled thermomechanical effects
- Phase transition or regime change → Sigmoidal functions of T indicating abrupt property changes at critical temperatures
- Elastic-to-plastic transition smoothing → tanh(c*epsilon) or similar smooth step to transition between elastic and plastic regimes
